My first 2 attempts were definitely user error, and apparently hair that had been previously shaved is extremely stubborn. 3rd time is a charm, right? I can't stress enoughthat when applying the sugar, the sugar absolutely must be proper consistency, paper thin, and in the correct direction, otherwise it doesn't grab the hair properly. My persistence paid off... 3rd time IS a charm... NO bruising, and NO hair! There was still some bleeding from some follicles, but only in the spots that I had missed previously. I expect there won't be bleeding next time around if the trend is consistent. Verdict: I gave Moom only 4 stars because the learning curve is a little painful, and I feel the instructions could be a bit better, but the video was definitely helpful. I highly recommend watching it before you start. I also feel that they should have included plastic applicators instead of wooden tongue depressors. I really like that it's all natural, and it's not as harsh as hot wax. Pros -It's gentle on the skin, so you can wax your skin multiple times without much irritation. I've heard you shouldn't wax the same place several times because you can tear off skin. The after is nothing like wax - it doesn't burn! -Moom only grabs onto your hair, not your skin, too. Unlike waxing, which also grabs live cells, Moom doesn't tear your skin. -You don't need to microwave it! Although it's easier to spread when it's warmer, it's still pliable at room temperature (75 degrees). -If you make a mistake, no problem! Unlike wax, which requires special oils to remove, Moom is made out of sugar, so it washes off very easily with water, which also allows you to reuse the cloth! -It grabs short hair! My hair is short and not course, but it grabbed hair that was less than a quarter of an inch, which is the recommended length for Moom. Cons -Like all hair removal products, it misses hair sometimes. But unlike wax, you can go back over with Moom instead of using tweezers. -Ok, I really can't think of anything else. A couple tips: -If you decide to warm up the wax by letting it float in hot water, make sure to put the Moom jar in the container, then fill the container up with water. I did the opposite (I put water in a bowl, then dropped the Moom jar in), and water got in the jar. Because Moom is made out of sugar, the water liquefied a chunk of Moom. I poured out the water and destroyed Moom from the jar, but we'll see if it still works in the next couple of month. -If you're waxing sensitive areas for the first time (like the bikini area), use the small strips designated for your eyebrows/lip/chin. -Make sure you pull the cloth as parallel to your skin as possible. It hurts less. Make sure you hold your skin taunt too, because it also reduces the pain. I usually don't write long reviews, but Moom is definitely the way to go!   87. this product works really well if you use it properly. i bought it to use on my bikini area but it works on finer facial hair as well. here are some tips for using the product: * make sure you're hair is in the right length range - 1/4\\" to 1/2\\" works best in my experience. if the hair is too long or short the product won't work. you can buy a beard/bikini trimmer to uniformly trim the hair to the right length. * wash the area before waxing (any lotions, natural oils, etc will interfere with the ability of the product to stick to the hair) * thoroughly dry the area before waxing and if necessary, keep a tissue with you to wipe off areas that may get wet/damp again (like underarms) * the wax consistency should be fluid, but don't overheat so it's like water * apply a thin coat - if it isn't you'll get a lot of pain and no hair removal * sometimes you'll get a little strip of hair that got the wax on it but wasn't pulled out. don't put more wax on it and try to pull it out again - move on to other areas, then wash and dry the areas that need to be gone over again and start fresh. when i do my (entire) bikini area i usually have to repeat the process three times to get all the little spots that didn't work the first time through. * if you're using this product on your bikini area and you've never waxed before, expect some mild to moderate pain the first time. by the third time the hair comes out really easily and the pain level is non-existent to mild, depending on the area. i also used this on my face and legs and never had any sort of pain, even the first time. overall i'm very pleased with this product, especially because the hair comes out easier the more you use it. the effect definitely does noteven come close to lasting for two months as the description says it can. for me it lasts about a week before the hair is noticeable, then takes about another half week to get long enough to wax again. i've done my legs and upper lip twice and my bikini area four times and have used about 3/4 of the jar so i'm ordering again. i'm getting the whole kit again because i need more strips but next time i'll just get the refill jar. great product at a great price.

  130. Hi, I wanted to share what I thought was a better way to use this product to get results you want.<br /><br /> Background: I'm Middle Eastern originally, and have been using sugar wax most of my life to remove hair, however it's always easier when someone does the waxing for you, as when you do it alone it can be very messy. But I was fed up of spending so much money on getting waxed and I decided to do it myself.<br /><br />Usually sugar wax is used at room temperature when you just want to do basic spreading and pulling (it's a technique you have to learn through observation, then trial and error).<br />But I liked Moom's idea of using a couple of extra tools ( spreading stick and cloths) to get the job done with less agony. And after a couple of sessions here and there, and much experience generally with sugar wax, I can say this is my favorite way to use this product:<br /><br />- Do not heat the wax in the Microwave as suggested by Moom, for centuries people have used sugar wax at room temperature. And I find this is best...as even when slightly heated it gets too sticky and cannot grab the hair as firmly. When at room temperature the wax can get a firmer grip of the hair without going all over the place in a messy way ( and hence is not as painful when pulling).<br /><br />- As opposed to spreading the wax on the hair directly (which I find can be messy and painful sometimes when the hair is slightly long), instead spread a thin layer of the wax on the cloth itself, making sure you have an area relative to that you're targeting on your body. So for bikini line, I'll spread a thin layer on the cloth, that is long and somewhat wide. I've used the smaller cloths for smaller areas. Note: it's more manageable to spread thin layer of wax on the cloth than it is on your body, especially for smaller, more sensitive areas.<br /><br />- When you put the waxed cloth on the body part your targeting, just tap and rub it a few times gently, making sure its in place, that also slightly warms the wax. Then wait for like 2-3 seconds (gives time for the sugar to settle) and pull with a quick firm grip.<br /><br />So that's basically my favorite way of using this product, less messiness, less product wasting (for both the sugar and the cloths) and MUCH less pain.<br /><br />Hope this helps =)<br /><br />Side Note: Btw I only use this for my bikini area (the whole area) and sometimes under arms, for everything else I use an epilator machine.lso slightly warms the wax. Then wait for like 2-3 seconds (gives time for the sugar to settle) and pull with a quick firm grip.<br /><br />So that's basically my favorite way of using this product, less messiness, less product wasting (for both the sugar and the cloths) and MUCH less pain.<br /><br />Hope this helps =)<br /><br />Side Note: Btw I only use this for my bikini area (the whole area) and sometimes under arms, for everything else I use an epilator machine.

  180. First, for everyone complaining about the amount of product, please note that they also sell this in a 12 oz. size (which is the one I actually bought). This did the trick, and I started to see some hairs coming out. You definitely do have to go over most areas more than once, especially if your hairs grow in pretty random directions and not in much of a \\"pattern\\" like mine. It's very specific to the direction of your growth, if that makes any sense, more so than regular wax. I was disappointed to find out after my first session that I still ended up with the unsightly whiteheads the next day (and of course a few more in the days to follow). So I hit the internet up and came across a recipe for homemade Tend Skin - just search for it and you can make some too. I used it on my existing zits and they seemed to go away faster and I didn't see any new ones. I also came across some other promising things I could try my next time MOOMing.<br /><br />So this most recent session, I washed my face in warm water (to loosen up the pores and their grip on the hairs) and mild Dove soap first. I swabbed the area with a little alcohol first, and when this dried, applied a light dusting of powder so the MOOM would stick better. And when I used the MOOM, I applied AGAINST the hair growth (and rubbed on the cloth strip against the growth), and removed in the SAME direction as growth. Some websites I had visited stated that this was the correct way to do sugaring, and MOOM is really just a form of sugaring. I found that it removed the hair as well or betterthan last time, and it felt slightly gentler and less painful this way. I did small patches at time, also trying to let areas rest a bit before going back over them. After MOOMing, I washed the area again with COLD water (to close those infection-prone pores) and the same mild soap, dried the area, and applied the home-made Tend Skin solution (really just crushed up Asprin, witch hazel and alcohol). I am also planning on not touching the area at all, as I know this can contribute to pimples. It looks great this time, with minimal redness and almost no stray hairs, and feels clean and cool. I will keep my fingers crossed that no whiteheads come in - I have a good feeling about it though, I have to say!<br /><br />Oh, and it goes without saying that the cleanup with this stuff is waaaay easier than with wax, since it is water soluble. As everyone knows, no hair removal method is perfect (there is always a \\"catch\\") , but I am thinking that MOOM might be the lesser of the evils that I've been looking for.<br /><br />UPDATE! I've changed my rating from 4 to 2 stars. I thought I owed it to people to mention that I no longer use this stuff. I DID end up breaking out in whiteheads on my face, just as I had with regular hot wax. This, along with the fact that it doesn't remove hair quite as well as hot wax does, made this product a big disappointment for me. I'm back to depilatory cream for my upper lip, as it is the least disagreeable option I have tried. The cream I'm currently using doesn't get rid of all the hair like I wish it would, but at least it doesn't burn me like some have - I end up having to pluck a few stragglers, which kind of sucks, but it is the best option I've found. Laser hair removal has piqued my interest as of late, but that is another can of worms altogether...

  198. I just used this for waxing my bikini line. I'm new to waxing that area and I'm completely new to this kind of wax (I normally use wax strips for my upper lip). *Pain: When it comes to ripping your hair out, stinging is what I typically expect. But this stuff doesn't really burn or sting when you rip it off; it's kind of hard to describe. I'd say it's more of a pressure as you pull it off your skin. On a relative scale, tweezing, getting your blood drawn, pulling a Band-Aid off your arm, and those horrible Sally Hansen wax strips definitely hurt more than this. For some reason, I was terrified every time I was about to pull a strip off, but it was always underwhelming. *Effectiveness: It works provided you apply it properly. If you put it on too thick, it's not going to work. You've got to spread it out super thin (basically scrape the stuff off in the direction of the hair growth, leaving a very thin layer). It sometimes does leave a few stray hairs here and there, but it's no big deal -- just reapply (since it doesn't irritate the skin, this isn't a problem) or tweeze them out. I'd say it removes ~90% of the hair where you apply it. Easy to spread with the sticks (but you will have some long strings of honey from the jar to your body, so be prepared with a wet cloth to wipe your hands and any surfaces as necessary). I did the bikini area, which I assume is one of the most sensitive body parts, and yet I had very little pain. Really follow the directions and 1) don't use too much wax, just enough to spread it very thinly; 2) don't press down on the strips, just rub three times quickly; 3) don't overheat the wax... and the wax melts from the center so even though the bottle feels cool, the wax in the center can be hot; 4) trim the hair to 1cm, any longer and there might be some pain; and 5) spread in the direction of hair growth, and pull skin taut while pulling off strips in the opposite direction. The wax also wipes off really well with some warm water, so it was easy to clean my body, hands, sticks, and strips for next time. I only did it last night so I can't comment on the rate of regrowth, but so far I'm satisfied with the process and the results and there's still so much product left I think it'll last me at least 6 months or a year.   318. As someone who has been waxing my own legs for a couple of years, MOOM was easy and effective.<br /><br />Tips for the best hair follicle ripping experience:<br /><br />1. Ensure hair is 1/4&#34; - 1/2&#34; long otherwise lots of hairs will get left behind. Too short, and they wont get picked up.. too long and it'll just be a gross painful mess.<br /><br />1. Do some prepping before hand - the day before waxing, exfoliate skin to remove dead skin and moisturize lightly ( i like to use coconut oil)<br /><br />2. Have your area ready - lay out some paper towels or anything to catch sticky drips<br /><br />3. Heat the wax to a thick syrup like consistency - I find that when the consistency is like thick syrup - its easiest to spread thinly which helps pick up the hair best. Of course test this on your skin first - if you're sensitive to heat wait a bit longer.<br /><br />4. Spread wax thinly - spread the wax very thinly in the direction of hair growth. You want there to be a very thin and shiny coat, but not have it globby or streaky. Then immediately put the strip on, firmly press down in the direction of hair growth a couple times.<br /><br />5. Ripping the strip - with one hand, pull your skin taut in the opposite direction of hair growth, while the other hand quickly rips the strip off in the opposite direction of hair growth (just like ripping off a bandaid)<br /><br />If you've done this correctly, that should minimize the pain and the same strip can be used several more times (if there wasn't too much hair after the first rip)

  477. I started using this almost a year ago (and I still have about 1/4 of a jar left) and for a while I followed the package directions. It gets more hair in one go, it's easier to work with, and it doesn't hurt as much. Note that I use this on some very sensitive areas, so less pain is a big deal for me.<br /><br />Here's how I recommend using MOOM:<br />1. Don't heat the wax up. Spread it pretty thinly at room temperature onto a small strip of cloth, leaving some room to hold on.<br />2. Place the waxed strip on wherever you're hairy and press in, making sure to rub the back of the strip back and forth a few times. If you let the wax warm up too much, it'll pull less hair out.<br />3. Hold your skin taught and rip the strip off. Repeat as necessary.<br /><br />Also, you might want to buy some wooden craft sticks or tongue depressors from your local crafts section, because if you're waxing a small area, the couple of sticks that come in the package won't last you nearly as long as the jar of wax.

  512. Before purchasing this I tried a number of different waxing products. Hard wax, soft wax, wax strips. Until, I looked at the ingredients! If you have the items to make lemonade, you can make this yourself. And it is so incredibly easy. And a fraction of the cost! All you need is two cups of sugar, 1/4 cup lemon juice, and 1/4 cup of water. (You can add a couple drops of tea tree oil and chamomile but don't really notice a difference.) Mix it together and bring to a boil. Once its boiling, bring it down to a simmer and let it cook for 20 minutes until its a deep brown. Move it to an airtight container and let it cool. It will give you the EXACT same results!

It's difficult to see to do the backs of legs - you can do it but it would be really great if you had someone else to do those parts for you.<br /><br />I have not found out how long the results will last yet.   599. I love this stuff! I bought some years ago because I was sick and tired of spending an hour in the bathroom plucking my eyebrows one by one. Too time consuming and it was always painful. In that event, I do pop it in the microwave for 15-25 seconds and then wait for it cool down a bit before I use it on my skin. The muslin strips are also a nice touch. There are two sizes of strips- small and HUGE and I rarely ever need to use the latter. It includes two sizes of \\"applicators\\" as well which are really nothing more than wooden popsicle sticks or tongue depressors, again one set thin and the other wide (I use the thin one). The sticks and fabrics bits are easy to clean, just use soap and water and let them air dry.<br /><br />Moom is easy to apply, almost too easy. I'd caution anyone who uses it that LESS IS MORE! You can always remove more hair, you can't replace it once it's gone nearly as easily so take your time and apply with care. Oh yeah, remember to wash your face BEFORE you use it. You really do need to remove any natural oils otherwise it won't work nearly as well (I've forgotten a few times with frustrating results). And always have some moisturizer on hand afterwards to apply to the spots where hair was removed, it will be tender and might get dried out. Moisturizer will help that. Definitely recommended!
